    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6526449735124829063">Engelsfors. Vackert namn, risig stad. Omgiven av djupa skogar där människor ofta går vilse och försvinner. Sex tjejer har just börjat gymnasiet.   <span id="freeText6526449735124829063" style="display:none">Engelsfors. Vackert namn, risig stad. Omgiven av djupa skogar där människor ofta går vilse och försvinner. Sex tjejer har just börjat gymnasiet. De har inget gemensamt - förutom att en uråldrig ondska jagar dem.<br /><br />Höstterminen har just börjat när en elev hittas död på en av gymnasieskolans toaletter. Alla förmodar att det var ett självmord. Alla utom de som vet sanningen.<br /><br />En natt då månen färgats mystiskt röd förs sex tonårstjejer till den nedlagda folkparken. De vet inte hur de har kommit dit eller varför de är där, men utan varandra kommer de inte att överleva.<br /><br />De får veta att de är häxor. De Utvalda, som nämns i en uråldrig profetia. Plötsligt är gymnasiet på liv och död - bokstavligt talat. De måste lära sig samarbeta trots sina olikheter, och kontrollera de magiska krafter som vaknat till liv inom dem. Tiden håller på att rinna ut. De måste hitta och besegra ondskan som jagar dem, innan ondskan hittar dem.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6526449735124829063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1267558662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1267558662" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1267558662?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781468306583" href="/book/show/16101193-the-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=first-reads-giveaway">first-reads-giveaway</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1267558662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7479224263646562088"><i>The Circle</i> was an excellent and gritty urban fantasy. It was dark enough that I would hesitate to classify it as young adult. It is about a group of close friends and magic.<br/><br/>It reminded me of that 1996 film, <i>The Craft</i>, which, as you will recall, is about a group of angst-y high school friends who find out that they're witches and have to deal with all of the issues that go along with that. There's drama, danger and magic... oh my!<br/><br/>For such a large cast of characters, Strandberg does an amazing job</span>
  <span id="freeText7479224263646562088" style="display:none"><i>The Circle</i> was an excellent and gritty urban fantasy. It was dark enough that I would hesitate to classify it as young adult. It is about a group of close friends and magic.<br /><br />It reminded me of that 1996 film, <i>The Craft</i>, which, as you will recall, is about a group of angst-y high school friends who find out that they're witches and have to deal with all of the issues that go along with that. There's drama, danger and magic... oh my!<br /><br />For such a large cast of characters, Strandberg does an amazing job fleshing them all out. Each has their own unique feel, story, and interests. At first, I was concerned that I wouldn't be able to tell Vanessa from Linnea from Minoo but that never happened.<br /><br />Strandberg also deftly captures the high school girls' attitudes and hang ups. He makes you love each one of them with their failures and unrealized potential. I believed in the characters and was cheering for them the whole time. It takes talent to create that level of emotional bonding with a cast of protagonists. Strandberg nails it.<br /><br />There's a lot of surprises in store for the readers who pick this up. Not to spoil anything, but you may want to have some tissues around if you're a sensitive type.<br /><br />I think that the best part about this trilogy is that all three books have already been published. They were originally written in Swedish. It took a couple years to be translated into English, but aren't we lucky?<br /><br />Also, in early 2015, this book was made into a film so there's no waiting on that either. Awesome.<br /><br />For people with triggers or appropriate reading material concerns, there's some intense murder and cutting scenes, bullying, language, a near rape and a bunch of underage sex (but not overly graphic like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28678119.Paper_Princess__The_Royals___1_" title="Paper Princess (The Royals, #1) by Erin Watt" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Princess</a>). Mature young adults could probably handle it, probably 16+. It's up to the parents, but read responsibly.<br /><br />If you enjoyed <i>The Circle</i>, you may enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6101718.The_Magicians__The_Magicians__1_" title="The Magicians (The Magicians #1) by Lev Grossman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magicians</a> by Lev Grossman or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6881685.Bitter_Seeds__The_Milkweed_Triptych___1_" title="Bitter Seeds (The Milkweed Triptych, #1) by Ian Tregillis" rel="nofollow noopener">Bitter Seeds</a> by Ian Tregillis.<br /><br />I received a free copy of this book through Goodreads First Reads. FTC guidelines: check!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7479224263646562088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_252720501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252720501" />
    <a title="Mari - loves to read" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2357731-mari---loves-to-read"><img alt="Mari - loves to read" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323630005p2/2357731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252720501?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mari - loves to read" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mari - loves to read" href="/user/show/2357731-mari---loves-to-read">Mari - loves to read</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252720501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18377653725076208158"><b>Do you like reading novels that keeps you up into the wee hours of night?</b> If you do then make sure to read The Circle, it is a true page turner! The Circle is a young adult fantasy that pulls off something that very few fantasy novels manages to do, it manages to somehow be a kind of a contemporary novel at the same time.<br/><br/><br/><b>Sky high expectations</b> <br/>In the Nordic countries The Circle has been receiving so much praise that I was actually scared to read it. My expectations where sky high and needless to </span>
  <span id="freeText18377653725076208158" style="display:none"><b>Do you like reading novels that keeps you up into the wee hours of night?</b> If you do then make sure to read The Circle, it is a true page turner! The Circle is a young adult fantasy that pulls off something that very few fantasy novels manages to do, it manages to somehow be a kind of a contemporary novel at the same time.<br /><br /><br /><b>Sky high expectations</b> <br />In the Nordic countries The Circle has been receiving so much praise that I was actually scared to read it. My expectations where sky high and needless to say The Circle had a long way to fall if it did not meet my expectations. I’m delighted to announced that I DEVOURED The Circle and it is so far among my top 3 novels of 2012(I’ve read 50 so far so that’s saying something). <br /><br /><b>Realistic portrait of teenage life</b> <br />I was glued to the page from the very dramatic beginning, it starts out with a suicide and that was a bit difficult to read about(but that's life, it is not always easy). There is no sugarcoating in this novel, which is part of why I love it so much, this is real yet this is also fantasy. The fantasy element is almost more of a background figure in this first novel as we're zooming in on the characters and their life. I quite like that and I reckon the fantasy element of the story will be a lot more visible in the next two installments.<br /><br /><b>Multiple point of view - and it actually works incredibly well.</b> <br />Authors Mats Strandberg and Sara B. Elfgren have managed to create a great story with several “I-did-not-see-that-one-coming”- moments. The characters in this story are all very interesting and each of the six girls has got a unique gift that is important to the task at hand. It is drama time when six very different teenage girls are forced together in this way, and what a great drama it was! <br /><br />It is wonderful, as well as heartbreaking, to be able to get inside these girls head. We got a great variation of characters; the seemingly perfect girl, the victim, the quiet one, the kind one and more. It all resulted in me having to dry of tears from my cheeks several times during this read. I must add that one of the girls is a bit of a secret and it is quite clear that the readers will find out a lot more about her as the saga of The Chosen Ones continue on.<br /><br /><b>First in a trilogy - is there a cliffhanger ending?</b> <br />The Circle is the first book in a new trilogy and we all know how those books ends, right? Well The Circle does not end with the usual cliffhanger, we get some kind of a solution while we still have more than enough loose ends to know there will be a whole lot more to look forward to in the next installment.<br /><br /><b> Sex, drugs and Rock'N Roll - not quite but a tiny warning is called for.</b> <br />I might add that this book is perhaps most suitable for older teens as it contains both sex (nothing very graphic tough) and some talk of drinking and drugs. In my opinion this is the most real YA novel I’ve read of quite some time. Also the young adult in this novel is around 17-18 years old.<br /><br />I’m pretty sure that this trilogy will get a huge fan base consisting of both young adults and adults. <br /><br /><b>Also worth mentioning:</b> <br />This Swedish trilogy is translated into 21 languages.<br /><br />Did I manage to tempt you? Or did you not notice my enthusiasm there? ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18377653725076208158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15253676870810376370" style="display:none">4.5 Stars<br /><br />This book was truly a surprise to me. <div id="review_975654193" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/975654193" />
    <a title="Sarah Mac" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4490376-sarah-mac"><img alt="Sarah Mac" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499925811p2/4490376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/975654193?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Mac" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Mac" href="/user/show/4490376-sarah-mac">Sarah Mac</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781468306583" href="/book/show/16101193-the-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=read-regifted">read-regifted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-2015">zzz-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-2015-low-expectations">zzz-2015-low-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=mary-sue-puke-bucket">mary-sue-puke-bucket</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=impulse-shopping">impulse-shopping</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-departed-ya">zzz-departed-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer975654193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14369376117839972294">Eh, it's alright. [/Wodehouse]<br/><br/>This was a mixed bag, so let's be nice & start with the things I liked. (Sorry, but caffeine is failing me today. This will be a bullet review.)<br/><br/><br/>-Grittiness. I appreciated that these teenagers swore like normal people. I also liked (though perhaps it's the wrong word? :P) that they were open about drug use & sex. It felt realistic. <br/><br/>-Elemental magic. The Book of Patterns & its magical process was quite interesting, though both were continually pushed aside in favor of</span>
  <span id="freeText14369376117839972294" style="display:none">Eh, it's alright. [/Wodehouse]<br /><br />This was a mixed bag, so let's be nice &amp; start with the things I liked. (Sorry, but caffeine is failing me today. This will be a bullet review.)<br /><br /><br />-Grittiness. I appreciated that these teenagers swore like normal people. I also liked (though perhaps it's the wrong word? :P) that they were open about drug use &amp; sex. It felt realistic. <br /><br />-Elemental magic. The Book of Patterns &amp; its magical process was quite interesting, though both were continually pushed aside in favor of teen dwama. This magic isn't happy unicorns &amp; bunnies; it's ectoplasm &amp; spit &amp; drops of blood. There was a very earthy, grounded feel about the wicca scenes.<br /><br />-Vanessa. She was by far my favorite of the girls. I loved her Fuck You attitude &amp; unapologetic party girl behavior combined with normal human fluctuations re: family &amp; love; she was flamboyant &amp; likable despite her flaws.<br /><br /><br />...And now, the things I disliked:<br /><br />-Poorly intro'd supernatural powers. In contrast to the wicca scenes, the sudden onset of paranormal abilities didn't work. And WTF was that ending? I hate when authors wedge nebulous soul stuff into their magic. It feels like an excuse to create vague deus-ex-machina resolutions...which is exactly what happened here.<br /><br />-Minoo. Her actually looking like a Pre-Raphaelite painting when she thinks she's so hideous, her good grades &amp; family security setting her apart from the others, her trouble making friends, her shyness with boys -- yawn. And <i>of course</i> her magic ends up being the most powerful &amp; the least understood. What an annoying little Sue.<br /><br />-Anna-Karin. I don't care if she was bullied. That sucks, but it doesn't excuse her obnoxious passive-aggressive behavior.<br /><br />-The onslaught of minutely-described bleakness in everyday actions. Apparently this is an important ingredient in contemporary Swedish fiction, but I'll be damned if I see the allure. *blink*<br /><br />-Disappearing parent syndrome. But it wasn't just the parents -- all the adults in this town were either absent, drunk, or clueless. Whut? If the fate of the fucking world is at stake, why wouldn't some of the adults have understood what was going on &amp; tried to help? The only ones who knew about magic were either senile or too uninformed to actually help the girls.<br /><br />-Length. This book was at least 200 pages too long. End of story.<br /><br /><br />It was mildly entertaining &amp; better than other YAs, but I've no interest in reading the other books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14369376117839972294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_711249478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/711249478" />
    <a title="Lukas Anthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10117401-lukas-anthony"><img alt="Lukas Anthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486063394p2/10117401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/711249478?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lukas Anthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lukas Anthony" href="/user/show/10117401-lukas-anthony">Lukas Anthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781468306583" href="/book/show/16101193-the-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10117401-lukas-anthony?shelf=missed-the-koolaid">missed-the-koolaid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10117401-lukas-anthony?shelf=series-debut">series-debut</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711249478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12398515690532687277"> <b>This book is like a bad afternoon special.</b><br/><br/>I really wanted to like this book. I'd been looking for a witchy read lately and I thought this might do the trick, sadly it was not to be. Note to self; Never, EVER trust a blurb from now on. You see the blurb to this book makes it sound like some epic, saving the world supernatural story. On the back, it's compared to Buffy, The Secret Circle and even The Girl With The Dragon Tattoo. How is it then, that this is NOTHING like any of those? GWTDT especi</span>
  <span id="freeText12398515690532687277" style="display:none"> <b>This book is like a bad afternoon special.</b><br /><br />I really wanted to like this book. I'd been looking for a witchy read lately and I thought this might do the trick, sadly it was not to be. Note to self; Never, EVER trust a blurb from now on. You see the blurb to this book makes it sound like some epic, saving the world supernatural story. On the back, it's compared to Buffy, The Secret Circle and even The Girl With The Dragon Tattoo. How is it then, that this is NOTHING like any of those? GWTDT especially, I mean wtf? <br /><br />This novel is 600 pages of melodrama, with about 50 pages of actual witchcraft. That was my biggest gripe with the novel, the author doesn't at all seem concerned with the supernatural aspect in the slightest. All she seems to care about is 'teen issues'. This book is basically an unfunny, Mean Girls lite tale on the dangers of popularity. You see, each one of our 5 witches is from a different social group within their school, and ALL the author talks about is how they shouldn't be friends. Don't worry though, they will be bff's forever by the end, because that's what type of novel this is, a cheesy one. <br /><br />What little there is of a supernatural storyline is ridiculously generic, actually generic might be too kind a word. It basically plays out like a murder mystery, yet when the killer is finally revealed, I kid you not, it makes absolutely NO sense. None. Nada. Zilch. I felt like I'd missed a huge chunk of the novel, and was pulling possibly the biggest wtf? face I have ever pulled in my life. <br /><br />The author also seems to be OBSESSED with tackling every teen issue under the sun. You have some bullying, some anorexia, some abuse, some self-harm. I mean, do happy people even exist in this novel!? There were also far to many POV's, 6 characters share the limelight here, and they are all more or less interchangeable girls. This group needs a definite culling! One of them was also possibly the most annoying character I have ever read in YA. I didn't know it was physically possible to hate a fictional character this much! <br /><br />Honestly, I could complain about this novel for days, but I'm just going to leave it at that before I get really bitchy about it. Obviously, I do not recommend this one in the slightest. DON'T TRUST THE BLURB. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12398515690532687277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_778003206" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/778003206" />
    <a title="Monique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14772852-monique"><img alt="Monique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483841850p2/14772852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/778003206?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monique" href="/user/show/14772852-monique">Monique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/18193378-the-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=infinity-stars">infinity-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=five-plus-stars">five-plus-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=weird-strange-books">weird-strange-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=la-phone-books-big-books">la-phone-books-big-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=witchcraft-wicca-voodoo">witchcraft-wicca-voodoo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=sex-or-heavy-romance-scenes">sex-or-heavy-romance-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=wtf-endings">wtf-endings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=4-point-5">4-point-5</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=i-never-saw-that-coming">i-never-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14772852-monique?shelf=awesome-girl-heroine">awesome-girl-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer778003206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3686661345065240735"><b>Real Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I have been sitting here and staring at my computer for exactly 47 minutes trying to figure out how to start this review; so since I can not think of anything, this is what I shall give you<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380371075ra/724098.gif' width='300' height='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>It took me a while to actually pick up the book and read it, but I did and I am very glad I did. And it is <b>not</b> because I have anything against Swedish authors(I love Sweden <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385911411ra/7257441.gif' width='30' height='20' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>It's just that most of the time, whenever a book this size is published, it often gets patches of <i>booorrriinngg</i> and </span>
  <span id="freeText3686661345065240735" style="display:none"><b>Real Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br><br>I have been sitting here and staring at my computer for exactly 47 minutes trying to figure out how to start this review; so since I can not think of anything, this is what I shall give you<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380371075ra/724098.gif" width="300" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It took me a while to actually pick up the book and read it, but I did and I am very glad I did. And it is <b>not</b> because I have anything against Swedish authors(I love Sweden <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385911411ra/7257441.gif" width="30" height="20" class="gr-hostedUserImg">It's just that most of the time, whenever a book this size is published, it often gets patches of <i>booorrriinngg</i> and I just really didn't want to waste my time with a book that is so boring when I could be reading something awesome. Well, Sara B. Elfgren &amp; Mats Strandburg, you did not dissapoint.<br><br><b>Summary:</b> The Circle is about 6 girls-Minno, Vanessa, Linnea, Anna-Karin, Rebecka, and Ida-who are drawn be an invisible force to an abandoned amusement park during a blood-red moon after the apparent suicide of high school student Elias Malmgreen. Scared and angry, all the girls start to freak out and leave. Ida's body is then taken over by a mystical being and tells the girls that they are fated to fight an ancient evil that is hunting them and, with there guide Nicolaus, they must band together and stop it. As the weeks pass, the girls discover that ther have an unique ability and starts exploring their powers. The six girls are wildly different and definitely not friends...but they are the Chosen Ones.<br><br><b>The Plot:</b> The plot is very intriguing. Though the genre is Fantasy, I think it would be easily pass a mystery. In the beginning of the book, the plot is a wee bit <s>boring</s> slow, but what can you expect. It went from the forced murder/suicide of Elias in the first chapter and a witch being capture to moody teenage girls who are naive and oblivious to the world around them. It slowly increases in excitement through out the book (unlike books that are like lightswitches, switching on and off from memorizing to WTF). The Circle does switch through the other girls personalities with out labeling,but it isn't a nuisance. Infact, its was quite nice that it didn't <s>often</s> leave at an exciting part to a super annoying apart in which you have to wait 6 chapters inorder to find out what happened to the character. <br><br><b>The Setting:</b> There really isn't much to say about the setting. Obviously, it took place in Sweden. I couldn't pronouce any of the town names to save my soul (I would type them out, but I can't get the proper signs inorder to properly spell out the words). The settings were a wee bit boring, but I think that that is the way the author(s) wanted it to be.<br><br><b>CHARACTERS:</b><br><br>1.)<b>Minoo:</b> Minoo is the smart girl in the story. She is the girl that nobody hates but is always ignored. Minoo is one of the <i>main</i> main characters in the book. She is <i>in love</i> with her homeroom teacher Max. Minoo has an average self-esteem (she doesn't think herself pretty and considers herself a pizza-face but is somewhat content about who she is). She is one of the Chosen One's, but feels left out because she only discovers what she can do at the end while everybody else is discovering there powers quickly and can read there <i>Book of Patterns</i>.<br><br>2.)<b>Vanessa:</b> Vanessa is sort of the school slut. Though she doesn't sleep with a ton of people, she does have sex a lot, drinks a lot, yells a lot at her parents (which is sort of okay since her mother only seems to date worthless and controlling guys and her boyfriend during the book-Nicke-is no exception). She is dating this <s>loser</s> <s>wannabe pimp</s> <s>low-life</s> college drop-out/ drug dealer named Wille who she <s>claims</s> says she loves, but when she gets her fortune done, the lady says that their love won't last. You discover her ability quite early within the book. She is sort of in the popular crowd and loves herself, but is still insecure like basically any regular teenage girl.<br><br>3.)<b>Ida:</b> Ida is the popular, classic mean girl in the school who looks perfect. Her power is discovered later -near the middle-of the book. She is a <s>big</s> little bit of a kiss-up and only does what she thinks will benefit her own needs. So basically, if you have ever read about or watched the mean, popular cheerleader who picks on everbody else for fun, then you know what I am talking about.<br><br>4.)<b>Linnea:</b> Linnea is the bad girl. She is the one who has a crappy life, is always revenge-filled, and keeps everyone at a distance. She is probably the angriest one in the whole book since her best friend was Elias. Throughout the book, her powers are given to you in little snippets, leaving you guessing and wondering, but her power is ultimately revealed near the end of the book.<br><br>P.S. I guessed right <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/515286.gif" width="350" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Moving on...<br><br>5.)<b>Rebecka:</b> Rebecka is the leader in the group. Her power is announce early within the book. Rebecka has the perfect boyfreind, is super pretty, and almost everyone likes her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Though she is not as perfect as she seems since she has a eating disorder, there are rumours going around, but nothing is concrete to the other students. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> What happens to her is terrible since she was the second one to be killed--thrown of the school building.<br><br>6.)<b>Anna-Karin:</b> Saving the worst for last, Anna-Karin. Anna-Karin is the sad, quiet girl that is always bullied where ever she goes. Sometimes called the B.O. Ho, she is constantly trying to find ways to be invisible. She lives on a farm with her Grandpa and her lazy, smoking and complaining mother who always blames the fault on Anna-Karin. Now you might be wondering, this girl sounds miserable, why so harsh? Well since I said that you asked so kindly, I shall tell you. The first 1/3 of the book. Anna-Karin is drowning in self pity. Yes, I get it that you life isn't the best and yes, I get it that you spent your whole life being bullied, but that does not mean you can act like some kind of emo-Bella and mope and whine all the time. So half of the time, I was thinking of telling her to GTFO<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429881ra/861562.gif" width="350" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Yes, I know how you feel <br><br>Then after the blood-red moon, she finally gets some confidence, so I am like<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380424213ra/845649.gif" width="150" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>So I am thinking, maybe she will grow up, maybe she will stop being so depressing and stand up for herself. Huh. Boy was I wrong. Instead, Anna-Karin uses her powers into minipulating everyone into liking her.<br>And I am like<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385918333ra/7258765.gif" width="350" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Then when everybody tells her to stop, that it's inmoral to do that, she is all like<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385920861ra/7259084.gif" width="350" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>So 'till about near the end of the book, whenever her POV showed up, all I could think of is this<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395923ra/762837.gif" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>She also nearly rapes a guy into having sex with her then realizes it isn't right then stops, so I am like <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385019ra/743837.gif" width="250" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Then near the end, she has the nerve to feel sorry for herself........I hate you <br><br><b>SIDE CHARACTERS</b>: <br>In The Circle, I think the side characters would be Max, the principal, Nicolaus, and Mona Moonbeam. I know that there are many other side characters, but I picked the ones that I believe show up the most and are most important in the book. Lets start off with Max. Max is the young, hot teacher in the high school. Minoo has been in love with him since she first saw him. Though he plays a very vague role in the begining and middle of the book, his characters gets <b>major</b> attention near the end of the book. He is very mysterious, though comes off ordinary. I actually found myself enjoying the times when he and Minoo talked. The principal's role in this book was a little unnecessary, yet useful. I found myself always trying to figure out if she was the killer or just an innocent bystander. My guess was wrong, but hey, no one is perfect. The principal comes off as mean and strict, but later in the book, she really starts to care for the girls and you see who she really is. Nicolaus-a.k.a. the janitor- is the guide. He is sort of a reincarnation, of who, I don't know. His purpose in life is to help guide and protect the Chosen Ones in there journey to defeat the ancient evil. He is a wee bit pothetic at first, but hear me out, he does get better. The last one would have to be Mona. Mona is an old lady who owns the Crystal Cave-a new age shop basically. Though she is mentioned only a couple of times, her role is significant in the story. You get to find out more about her near the middle and end.<br><br><b>The Romance:</b> The romance is a wee bit confusing in this book. There is Rebecka &amp; Gustaf, the perfect couple. Then there is Ida who is jealous of Rebecka because she has feelings for Gustaf ("G" is what she calls him). Then there is Minoo and Max, but the relationship should be wrong and inappropiate, but yet you still find yourself secretely rooting for them. And there is Vanessa and Wille, though Vanessa deserves way better than a drug dealer, she still loves him. But there is also the fortune that says that Vanessa and Wille's love won't last. There are also a few suggestions that Linnea and Vanessa might get together. Then there is Anna-Karin *gag* that is manipulating tons of dudes into liking her, especially this one hot *cue eyeroll* boy named Jari. And the girls parents relationships are all jacked up and out of whack. The romance sort of gives the book a soap opera feeling to the book, though not in a bad way. There was sex in the book, but not at all detailed and <i>ADULT</i> rated.<br><br><b>Overall:</b> The Circle was a really great read. It kept me on my toes. I can't wait to read the sequel "Fire".<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380754849ra/3119939.gif" width="350" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I agree weird nodding man, I agree...</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1080561596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5219814359168280186">I don't usually read YA, partly because I'm OA myself and partly because I find the often "simplified" language and more disturbingly simplified characters to be distracting. I did, however, take this on since my wife asked me to - she wanted another opinion about it, since she has her students adding it to their reading list. <br/><br/>I was partly pleasantly surprised - there are quite a few plot turns and character traits that you probably wouldn't expect - but partly my prejudice showed far too true. </span>
  <span id="freeText5219814359168280186" style="display:none">I don't usually read YA, partly because I'm OA myself and partly because I find the often "simplified" language and more disturbingly simplified characters to be distracting. I did, however, take this on since my wife asked me to - she wanted another opinion about it, since she has her students adding it to their reading list. <br /><br />I was partly pleasantly surprised - there are quite a few plot turns and character traits that you probably wouldn't expect - but partly my prejudice showed far too true. In the group of - initially unknowing - witches, we meet quite an interesting character gallery and the good-bad, black-white is not quite as well defined as is my experience with these books. But then there's the only male witch - he's gay - because gay boys are in touch with their feelings I guess. And also, teen girls have sex to numb the pain in their souls and as part of self-loathing and angst and self-punishment. Teen boys have sex because they're horny.<br /><br />Before you bite my head off, I'm not saying these things are probably not true in many cases, but ladling out stereotypes are usually considered a no-no, so why not break some new ground even in this area?<br /><br />Also, and I'm thinking this is due to US movies influences, drug use and alcohol abuse is described and consequences thereof are neglected, which I really don't see as a good thing. <br /><br />Anyway, I did like the book as a whole and I think I would have enjoyed it even more as a teenager, so for the YA readers I recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5219814359168280186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171707272" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1171707272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2397484641838406138">Where do I even beginning talking about this book? Do I start with the amazing characters? Or maybe the intriguing plot? Or maybe the insane need to know <i>more</i> it creates. I carried this book with me the entire day and I read it faster than I’ve read a book in …. I can’t even remember how long.<br/><br/>After the apparent (and graphic) suicide of young Elias in the school bathrooms, six girls come to realise that there is more to this world than it seems. Deemed “the Chosen Ones”, these girls learn of a pr</span>
  <span id="freeText2397484641838406138" style="display:none">Where do I even beginning talking about this book? Do I start with the amazing characters? Or maybe the intriguing plot? Or maybe the insane need to know <i>more</i> it creates. I carried this book with me the entire day and I read it faster than I’ve read a book in …. I can’t even remember how long.<br /><br />After the apparent (and graphic) suicide of young Elias in the school bathrooms, six girls come to realise that there is more to this world than it seems. Deemed “the Chosen Ones”, these girls learn of a prophesy in which their witchiness is to play a vital part. Now if they could only learn to get along!<br /><br />These girls are the very definition of an eclectic mix. We have Minoo, the nerd from the right side of the tracks. She has a hopeless crush on her teacher yet keeps her peers at bay. She refuses to get to close. There’s Rebecka, the popular girl who became popular when she started dating the popular guy. Struggling with an eating disorder, she lives in fear of the day when her perfect boyfriend realises she’s not good enough. Anna Karin is the frumpy, bullied girl that wants to be invisible. The only time she’s happy is when she’s at home with her animals, or with her eldery grandfather whom she adores. Enter mean girl Ida, the bully. She is a terrible person, but she’s human. You’ll grow to love her. Vanessa, the “slut”. She has a steady, drug dealing boyfriend and absolutely loathes her step father. And last but definitely not least, Linnéa. Outcast. The “addict”. She was Elias’ sister in all but blood, and the first one to be certain that his death was not a suicide. THEY’RE ALL PERFECT IN THEIR IMPERFECTIONS DON’T EVEN LOOK AT ME.<br /><br />The beginning may get a little confusing for some as you’re introduced to this ragtag bunch of characters, but it’s so incredibly worth it. They butt heads. A lot. It’s awesome.<br /><br />We can’t forget about dear Nicolaus, their guide through this whole mess. The only catch is, he knows less than they do! And he’s kind of a few fries short of a Happy Meal if you know what I mean. Poor guy.<br /><br />PLOT! OY THE PLOT! Get ready to spend a few hours on the edge of your seat my friends. It’s going to be a wild ride. Up. Down. East. Hell. Forwards. Sideways. All the places. Things happen that will leave you all “?!?!??!??!” and “!!?!?!?!!?!?!!”. <br /><br />Also, it has to be mentioned that one of my favourite things about this book was it’s realness. I can hear you groan: “Rebecca, it’s a fantasy. What are you talking about?” But no, hear me out okay. These teenagers are not perfect. Their lives are not romanticised. They have acne and weight issues and self esteem issues and family issues. You have drugs, alcohol, bullying, eating disorders, suicide and just a whole bunch of not-pretty things. Once again, it’s awesome.<br /><br />This book is translated from it’s original Swedish (duh) and honestly I could barely even tell. Also there’s a movie?? So if anyone can direct me to the English dub or some subtitled that’d be sweet.<br /><br />ONWARDS TO THE NEXT BOOK.</span>

<div id="review_670724478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/670724478" />
    <a title="Emm (Booksprite)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21182327-emm-booksprite"><img alt="Emm (Booksprite)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561018423p2/21182327.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emm (Booksprite)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emm (Booksprite)" href="/user/show/21182327-emm-booksprite">Emm (Booksprite)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21182327-emm-booksprite?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21182327-emm-booksprite?shelf=signed">signed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer670724478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4731285685479178843">March 2020:<br/>I can’t believe it’s been five years since I last visited this world. This trilogy continues to be my favorite, EVER, and I’m sure part of that is nostalgia (after all - it’s been almost ten years since it came out, WHAT??) but it truly is such a well crafted story. I don’t really have anything to add about the story that I didn’t say five years ago so let me just say that getting sucked into this would was the best reading cure slump ever. I’m gonna jump straight into Eld now!<br/><br/>Februar</span>
  <span id="freeText4731285685479178843" style="display:none">March 2020:<br />I can’t believe it’s been five years since I last visited this world. This trilogy continues to be my favorite, EVER, and I’m sure part of that is nostalgia (after all - it’s been almost ten years since it came out, WHAT??) but it truly is such a well crafted story. I don’t really have anything to add about the story that I didn’t say five years ago so let me just say that getting sucked into this would was the best reading cure slump ever. I’m gonna jump straight into Eld now!<br /><br />February 2015:<br />Let me just start this off by saying that this is my favorite book series ever - at the very least, it's my favorite Swedish series ever. I read this book for the first time about a month after it came out, in the springtime of 2011. Then I re-read it just before its sequel came out a year later. Since then, I've only re-read the sequel and read the final book when it came out in late 2013. In other words, it's been almost 1,5 years since I last visited Engelsfors, and almost three years since the last time I read this book. <br />And it was just as magical this time around as the previous ones. Cirkeln (or 'The Circle') is the kind of book that never loses its charm, no matter how many times you read it. It's such an incredible story - the characters are very diverse - you relate to at least some of the main characters, and the supporting characters also feel like people you've met in real life. The story is fascinating - it's exciting and you always want to keep reading, even when nothing noteworthy is happening. There's just enough amount of foreshadowing - nothing is obvious, but when things are revealed you easily find points in the plot from earlier that point toward the very thing that was revealed, and I just love that. I have a lot of other things to say about this book like the way it's written, that somehow differs from other Swedish YA novels and makes it unique and awesome, and how nice it is to read something that actually takes place in my home country and not the US. But that'll have to wait, because I really really want to make a video review of this. My love for this trilogy is just gigantic, and it has such a special place in my heart &lt;3<br /><br />If you're still reading, I just want to say that this book really deserves more hype internationally. I have yet to read this book in English (because yes, I own it in English as well), but if the Ruby Red trilogy could get BookTube hype, so can The Circle. It (and it's even better sequels) are just that good. Please read it if you can!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4731285685479178843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1127495653888938036">I bought this at a second hand book sale. Originally I only went to the second hand sale because a warehouse clearance proved to be extremely disappointing - barely anything that fitted my niche. The only reason I picked this up was because it has the same name as another book I my shelf. I just thought I was a different cover.<br/><br/>The reviews were mostly favourable, in fact I recall one of them calling this book the Scandinavian version of 'the craft'. *sigh* I loved that movie. This books was more </span>
  <span id="freeText1127495653888938036" style="display:none">I bought this at a second hand book sale. Originally I only went to the second hand sale because a warehouse clearance proved to be extremely disappointing - barely anything that fitted my niche. The only reason I picked this up was because it has the same name as another book I my shelf. I just thought I was a different cover.<br /><br />The reviews were mostly favourable, in fact I recall one of them calling this book the Scandinavian version of 'the craft'. *sigh* I loved that movie. This books was more then that though, sure it was about witches in high-school, but it was a little darker. A little bloodier.<br /><br />While it may have a few tiny errors (as quite a few works in translations do), I adored the story. Girls from completely different backgrounds were drawn together, and unlike other books, the girls quite realistically aren't best friends after a couple months of being forced together. They're still a work in progress (as the rest of us are as well).</span>
  <a data-text-id="1127495653888938036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_984130836" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984130836" />
    <a title="Wealhtheow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow"><img alt="Wealhtheow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1178337774p2/76129.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/984130836?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wealhtheow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wealhtheow" href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow">Wealhtheow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781468306583" href="/book/show/16101193-the-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer984130836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8228646848564562916">In the little town of Engelsfors, powers awaken in seven high school students. But even as they explore their new abilities, a malevolent force hunts them, one by one.<br/><br/>Lev Grossman wrote a blurb describing this as "The Circle is Twilight by way of The Girl With the Dragon Tattoo," which is the best proof anyone could need that he's a hack who doesn't actually read the books he references. The only resemblance between Twilight and the Circle is that they're both written for a YA audience, and the </span>
  <span id="freeText8228646848564562916" style="display:none">In the little town of Engelsfors, powers awaken in seven high school students. But even as they explore their new abilities, a malevolent force hunts them, one by one.<br /><br />Lev Grossman wrote a blurb describing this as "The Circle is Twilight by way of The Girl With the Dragon Tattoo," which is the best proof anyone could need that he's a hack who doesn't actually read the books he references. The only resemblance between Twilight and the Circle is that they're both written for a YA audience, and the only resemblance between TGWTDT and The Circle is that they were written in Swedish. The Circle is actually more like The Craft crossed with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13497818.The_Casual_Vacancy" title="The Casual Vacancy by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">The Casual Vacancy</a>. Some of the witches have crushes or relationships, but the focus of this book is on the claustrophobic feeling of a small town with a depressed economy and a high school riddled with cliques. To some of the witches, their powers offer them a way out--Anna-Karin finally has a way to not only protect herself against the bullies who have made her life hell, but turn the tables on them. But for most of the witches, having powers changes nothing at all. And for one, it makes matters far worse. <br /><br />I was impressed at how quickly each of the characters distinguished themselves. I found the first chapter or so confusing, but from then on had no difficulty telling each of the (many) main characters apart. I loved seeing all the facets of their lives, the differences between their school personas and their home selves and their inner personalities. I came to really like each of them (except Ida, ugh, but I gotta respect an author who's brave enough to have at least someone that unlikable), even though the book doesn't shy away from showing their selfish, narrow-minded, or foolish moments. And I really liked the friendships that developed between some of them. They felt like real friendships, not just opportunities for witty banter.<br /><br />The magic in this isn't what I'm used to; I expected wand waving or sympathetic magic and instead got rituals that use spit and gooey ectoplasm. <br /><br />The adult characters in this book are fascinating. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The school janitor declares himself the witches' protector, but he can't remember enough to actually help them, and there are hints that he comes from a far-off time. I liked the twist on the magic Council--interfering busybody bureaucrats I'm used to, but after all the threats I was as surprised as the witches when it turned out the Council was far less powerful and knowledgeable than it pretended. And I liked that the Big Bad wasn't pure evil, but had his own reasons for action. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I look forward to the next in the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8228646848564562916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1171976610" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171976610" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26267643-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403235328p2/26267643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1171976610?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/26267643-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781468308198" href="/book/show/18114365-the-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1171976610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8490045157475650710">May contain slight spoilers.<br/>COVER: I was immediately drawn to the cover. It's different from any other cover I've seen in a while. It's beautiful and interesting and it got me very excited to dive into the book.<br/>5/5<br/>PLOT: I think the premise of the novel is great. I love the witchy feel, especially considering it's a little darker than most of the supernatural novels circulating around. In a way, it's really gritty and dirty and sloppy but it still remains tasteful and realistic. I really liked th</span>
  <span id="freeText8490045157475650710" style="display:none">May contain slight spoilers.<br />COVER: I was immediately drawn to the cover. It's different from any other cover I've seen in a while. It's beautiful and interesting and it got me very excited to dive into the book.<br />5/5<br />PLOT: I think the premise of the novel is great. I love the witchy feel, especially considering it's a little darker than most of the supernatural novels circulating around. In a way, it's really gritty and dirty and sloppy but it still remains tasteful and realistic. I really liked that part of it.<br />5/5<br />CHARACTERS: <br />Elias-Elias is a character we don't see much of, considering he kills himself in the first chapter. But, he remains important throughout the whole novel.<br />Nicolaus-While not the most prominent character, I still loved him. I thought he was well-rounded and natural without being flat.<br />Minoo- Minoo reminded me of Hermione Granger in away. Everyone believes she's a know it all (sound familiar?) she's a self proclaimed ugly duckling who turns out to be a beauty (ringing any bells? Any at all?) she's a witch, and a more powerful witch then anyone, herself included, imagined (she's basically Hermione and no one will make me believe otherwise) <br />Vanessa- Vanessa is the typical party girl. Her family life is complicated, her boyfriend is a drug dealer, and she is kind of a bitch. as it turns out, her character is deeper and more relatable than I had anticipated. <br />Linnéa- for about half of the novel all we know about her is that she was a Elias' best friend, she is Gothic, and extremely closed off. Actually, she is a Mystery even when we think we know her. This made me really like her character. <br />Rebecka- Rebecka is a girl that we all know. She is frustratingly beautiful, and it's so nice and considerate it's impossible to hate her. She does have a secret though, a secret that greatly affects her character and the direction of the story.<br />Anna-Karin- I think we can all relate to Anna at least a little bit. She's self-conscious, friendless, and horribly bullied. At first I was positive I would love her, but she ended up being my least favorite character. Everything she did was extreme, and she spent the majority of the novel doing the exact opposite of what she needed to do. I found her character beyond frustrating.<br />Ida- remember how I said Vanessa was kind of a bitch? Well, Ida is the biggest bitch of them all. She is the popular mean girl we all know and hate.<br />4/5<br />PACING: this book was long, 596 pages to be exact. I love long books, but I felt that some of the scenes could have been tighter. Sometimes I felt they could have been cut altogether. I was curious to see what would happen next, but I could easily put the book down. On the bright side, the action scenes were perfectly paced to me. They didn't feel rushed, yet they didn't drag. They were my favorite part of the book in some cases. <br />3/5 <br />GENERAL COMMENTS: The writing was rather stale, but I think a large part of that was because it had been translated to English from Swedish. Other than that, I think the book has a lot of potential, but in some ways it fell flat. I'm not sure what was disconnectingwith me, but I was not as into it as I anticipated. It did have some great moments though. I really enjoyed the minor characters and thought they were interesting. My favorite part of the book though, was that I never really knew what was going on or what would happen next. <br />3/5 <br />Overall I enjoyed this book, I would recommend it to anyone who enjoys darker stories with the perfect amount of supernatural events and realistic characters. I will continue the rest of the trilogy.<br />Average: 4/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="8490045157475650710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17621887155466419969">My Summary: In a little town surrounded by trees, six teenaged girls begin to experience strange phenomena. Terrified and confused after the death of a fellow classmate, the six are drawn to an abandoned fairground on the night of a red moon. There they are told that they are witches - members of a "circle". Each has their own unique power, and it is their job to utilize their power and stop whatever is killing their friends.<br/><br/>But the girls don't take this warning seriously, choosing instead to ig</span>
  <span id="freeText17621887155466419969" style="display:none">My Summary: In a little town surrounded by trees, six teenaged girls begin to experience strange phenomena. Terrified and confused after the death of a fellow classmate, the six are drawn to an abandoned fairground on the night of a red moon. There they are told that they are witches - members of a "circle". Each has their own unique power, and it is their job to utilize their power and stop whatever is killing their friends.<br /><br />But the girls don't take this warning seriously, choosing instead to ignore what they've been told. As a result, one of their own is brutally murdered by the mysterious evil.<br /><br />Now, with one less member and only so much time left, these polar opposites must band together in order to control their abilities and destroy the evil haunting their town.<br /><br />My Thoughts: The Circle was one of those novels that made me sit back and stare blankly into space after I finished. I loved every minute of it! The authors have truly hit the jackpot with the slow-to-build plot and their ability to mix both contemporary issues with the paranormal - each character was complex and real, and you really felt like you got to know each and every one. This novel was the perfect book for fall - a lot of horror and paranormal, set in a spooky small town. A winning recipe. I devoured it.<br /><br />What I loved most was the insane twists and turns. Usually with paranormal books I can usually predict what is going to happen, but when it came to The Circle I was at a loss (in a good way!). It kept me up late into the night reading, but I regret nothing.<br /><br />Final Thoughts: If you're looking for a great Autumn read or just love a good paranormal YA mystery, check out The Circle. </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer3202147706560249283">If I had of read this when I was 14 my star rating would have been 5 stars. Unfortunately I’m a little bit* older than that, which means that some of the themes missed the mark for me personally. I really would recommend it to younger readers, as I feel like it would speak to them on a different level.<br/><br/>Almost every single stereotypical teenage problem is covered in this book. Drug use, drinking, suicide, self harm, sex, anorexia, low self esteem, bullying, being “different”, relationships with mu</span>
  <span id="freeText3202147706560249283" style="display:none">If I had of read this when I was 14 my star rating would have been 5 stars. Unfortunately I’m a little bit* older than that, which means that some of the themes missed the mark for me personally. I really would recommend it to younger readers, as I feel like it would speak to them on a different level.<br /><br />Almost every single stereotypical teenage problem is covered in this book. Drug use, drinking, suicide, self harm, sex, anorexia, low self esteem, bullying, being “different”, relationships with much older guys, inappropriate relationships with teachers - it felt like an episode of Degrassi: The Next Generation. The only thing not covered was teen pregnancy, but I don’t doubt that it may be covered in one of the other books in the series.<br /><br />The language also missed the mark for me. I’m not sure if some of the complexity of the prose was lost when it was translated to English, but when the word “chugalug” is used as a verb and the phrase “popping my cherry” is uttered by a character I can’t help but cringe.<br /><br />I found the characters to be a bit one dimensional, with not enough character development. In saying that, I did really like the realistic portrayal of the fraught nature of interactions between teenagers. The girls have this massive thing that connects them, but they don’t become best friends because of it. They still pretty much hate each other. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br />*Ok, a lot older</span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=magic">magic</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1182917600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13974563760115792250">The Circle is a Swedish Young Adult novel. Set in the small town of Engelsfor in Sweden, The Circle follows six teenagers at the local high school that find out they have magic powers.<br/><br/>For the first few chapters I was a little confused by all the different characters as the viewpoint jumps between the girls, but by the middle of the book I had them sorted. They are all very different and there is enough character development to start getting to know each of them.<br/><br/>Not all of the girls were very lik</span>
  <span id="freeText13974563760115792250" style="display:none">The Circle is a Swedish Young Adult novel. Set in the small town of Engelsfor in Sweden, The Circle follows six teenagers at the local high school that find out they have magic powers.<br /><br />For the first few chapters I was a little confused by all the different characters as the viewpoint jumps between the girls, but by the middle of the book I had them sorted. They are all very different and there is enough character development to start getting to know each of them.<br /><br />Not all of the girls were very likeable and they didn't get on with each other, this conflict and the regular action keeps the book moving nicely. <br /><br />There wasn't enough use of their magic powers for me though, for most of the book the girls struggled to understand what they were and had no real idea how to use them. It might be more realistic this way, but I want to see more magic! <br /><br />It's long for a young adult book, but it all wraps up nicely at the end, no cliff hangers here! So even though there are sequels this can be read as a one off. <br /><br />I will be reading the next book though, I want to see them getting the hang of their magic powers and using them a bit more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13974563760115792250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12965065212722115205">Trigger Warnings for depictions of suicide, cutting, eating disorders, pedophilia. <br/><br/>1.5 stars<br/><br/>I'm going to be completely honest, the only reason I didn't DNF this was because I DNFed the last book I 'read' and didn't feel like DNFing two books in a row. That being said, I skimmed the hell out of the last half of the book to the point where I missed the LGBT rep that's apparently in here somewhere? No idea where. Didn't see it. <br/><br/>The pacing of this story is awful, and the plot is so thin to the point</span>
  <span id="freeText12965065212722115205" style="display:none">Trigger Warnings for depictions of suicide, cutting, eating disorders, pedophilia. <br /><br />1.5 stars<br /><br />I'm going to be completely honest, the only reason I didn't DNF this was because I DNFed the last book I 'read' and didn't feel like DNFing two books in a row. That being said, I skimmed the hell out of the last half of the book to the point where I missed the LGBT rep that's apparently in here somewhere? No idea where. Didn't see it. <br /><br />The pacing of this story is awful, and the plot is so thin to the point of being almost non-existent. The synopsis of this book was so intriguing, but that moment doesn't happen until well over 100 pages into the story. The magical/paranormal element of this story then doesn't show up again for another 100 pages. Basically this book is 5% paranormal, 10% murder mystery, and 85% Mean Girls. I was expecting a little bit of Mean Girls. I was not expecting Mean Girls with just a touch of fantasy and murder mystery. I would not have picked this up had I realized this was basically about every teen issue the author could imagine. <br /><br />There were also way too many characters introduced way too quickly. I know there's a wide cast of main characters, but there were also so many minor characters. It was hard enough differentiating the main characters, but then I kept forgetting who these side characters were. <br /><br />Not at all what I was expecting. The cover and synposis made me think this was going to be a dark, paranormal fantasy with a cast of teen girls who have to solve their differences and work together. And we sort of get that, but it's more, a cast of teen girls sort of get powers but mostly just have teen drama that is made a bit worse cause hey teens keep getting murdered, but let's focus on this weird love triangle a bit more instead. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12965065212722115205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1281720538" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Therese" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6570538-therese"><img alt="Therese" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566735880p2/6570538.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3151392016977133366">This has been on my shelf for over four years now. And to be honest, I didn't think I would ever read it. But late last year I made a decision to stop buying so many books and just read the ones already on my shelves, so last week it was this book's turn to be read.<br/><br/>And you now what?   <span id="freeText3151392016977133366" style="display:none">This has been on my shelf for over four years now. And to be honest, I didn't think I would ever read it. But late last year I made a decision to stop buying so many books and just read the ones already on my shelves, so last week it was this book's turn to be read.<br /><br />And you now what? This book is <i>really good</i>. I did not think I would like it as much as I did, but here we are.<br /><br />The book just deliveries exactly what it promises. If you want a book about teen girls discovering that they're witches with a small town setting, you'll most likely really enjoy this book. The writing is solid. The characters are real and interesting. I could relate so much to them, especially Minoo (except for the whole "crush on a teacher" thing). They found out that they had to work together, and didn't immediately become best friends or anything. By the end of the book they still don't trust each other completely, and that makes sense, because learning to trust other people takes time, especially when some of these girls already have a complicated history with each other.<br /><br />All around a great piece of scandinavian YA literature.<br /><br />I will definitely read the next book in this series, and I can't wait until I've read enough of my already owned books so I can buy new ones without feeling guilty.</span>
