<div id="review_1591650866" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1591650866" />
    <a title="Esther (Chapter Adventures)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8666258-esther-chapter-adventures"><img alt="Esther (Chapter Adventures)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467756991p2/8666258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1591650866?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Esther (Chapter Adventures)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Esther (Chapter Adventures)" href="/user/show/8666258-esther-chapter-adventures">Esther (Chapter Adventures)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781468306583" href="/book/show/16101193-the-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1591650866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2019858890910452129"><a href='https://chapteradventures.wordpress.com/2016/06/29/review-the-circle-by-sara-bergmark-elfgren-mats-strandberg/' rel='nofollow noopener'> You can also see the review on my blog. </a><br/><br/>The Circle is an enjoyable easy read with a group of distinct main characters that happen to be Swedish teenage witches! Sadly, there isn’t much action or magic, but the little there is, I really liked. We spend a lot of time getting to know the lives of the girls and their growing relationship, which was very well done. I want to continue with the trilogy because I think there’s a lot of potential and the characters ended up captivating me.<br/><br/>I recently rea</span>
  <span id="freeText2019858890910452129" style="display:none"><a href="https://chapteradventures.wordpress.com/2016/06/29/review-the-circle-by-sara-bergmark-elfgren-mats-strandberg/" rel="nofollow noopener"> You can also see the review on my blog. </a><br /><br />The Circle is an enjoyable easy read with a group of distinct main characters that happen to be Swedish teenage witches! Sadly, there isn’t much action or magic, but the little there is, I really liked. We spend a lot of time getting to know the lives of the girls and their growing relationship, which was very well done. I want to continue with the trilogy because I think there’s a lot of potential and the characters ended up captivating me.<br /><br />I recently realized how much I enjoy books with different points of views. I think it can work wonders for character explorations and this is no exception. We get <b>three main points of views</b>, though there are more main characters than that. Since this book is about a group of witches that couldn’t be more different to one another having to come together to fight evil, it was really fun and also enlightening to read how one girl perceived the other, or what was happening in someone’s life when the others were struggling with different things. At first it was hard to distinguish between the girls, but as you read on, you start to see how <b>they all have a very unique personality and knowing them was my favorite part of reading this</b>. I liked how their weaknesses and strengths were very clearly exposed and how much they grow throughout this first novel. My favorite of all the girls was Vanessa.<br /><br /><blockquote>Just as siblings don’t choose each other, the Chosen Ones haven’t either. And, like siblings, they have to learn to live with each other.</blockquote><br /><br /><b>The themes were extremely varied.</b> Of course there’s magic (each girl has a power), but sometimes I felt it was more about teenage issues than witches issues. I really enjoyed how all the themes were treated. We have friendship and relationships in general (with their families and with their partners), self-doubt, suicide, grief, eating disorders, trust, sex, drugs, and probably more that are not coming to mind right now. <b>Despite having such heavy topics, they were address pretty gracefully and they never came off as too bleak or too graphic.</b> Also, there was a hint to an LGBTQIA+ relationship, but I won’t spoil it.<br /><br /><blockquote>She cannot take away their grief, but she can share it.</blockquote><br /><br />The <b>plot</b> was interesting because I wanted to know more about the characters, but as I said, a lot of magic was missing. Still, the bits we get are cool and darker than I expected and I can’t wait to discover more about it. <b>I loved seeing the relationship between the girls develop and how they tackled the issues in their lives.</b> I found the villain, among a few other things, very predictable and their motivations were a little confusing, but the way they attacked was the perfect amount of scary and dangerous. It all wrapped up quite nicely, which I appreciated.<br /><br /><blockquote>Because that’s how things are in this stupid town. You’re only what everyone thinks you are.</blockquote><br /><br /><b>As for the writing… </b>Well, I’m on the fence about it. It was plain, hence easy to read. That made the pages fly by. There was a good balance between the descriptions, the dialogues and the inner monologues, but there was something missing. It lacked personality. Maybe it’s because it’s hard to come up with a cohesive writing style between two authors. Whenever the characters entered a room, instead of a description to bring the place to life it almost sounded like an inventory!<br /> <br />Overall, The Circle was <b>an enjoyable read with great characters and complex themes and relationships</b>. I will continue reading the trilogy, but I hope the lack of magic, the predictability and the writing style improves because I think it has a lot of potential!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2019858890910452129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1289368644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289368644" />
    <a title="Joshua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17275548-joshua"><img alt="Joshua" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289368644?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshua" href="/user/show/17275548-joshua">Joshua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289368644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16018498824529385264">WOW! What an amazing book this was. And it’s all the more amazing because it really shouldn’t have been amazing. Considering its massive length, the sheer number of POV characters, and all the angst said POV characters go through, the chances of this being a good book were slim. And yet it was not just a good book, but a superlatively good book. With an exciting plotline, three-dimensional characters, intriguing balance between contemporary and fantasy YA, and sheer quality, The Circle captivate</span>
  <span id="freeText16018498824529385264" style="display:none">WOW! What an amazing book this was. And it’s all the more amazing because it really shouldn’t have been amazing. Considering its massive length, the sheer number of POV characters, and all the angst said POV characters go through, the chances of this being a good book were slim. And yet it was not just a good book, but a superlatively good book. With an exciting plotline, three-dimensional characters, intriguing balance between contemporary and fantasy YA, and sheer quality, The Circle captivated me from beginning to end.<br /><br />The Circle is reminiscent of what would happen if Buffy the Vampire Slayer was crossed with the Breakfast Club. In a small town in Sweden, six girls from vastly different backgrounds must unite to defeat ancient evil while unlocking their own magical powers. There’s also a murderer on the loose, using mind control magic to kill teenagers and make it look like suicide. It becomes rapidly clear that the so-called authority figures are either unable or unwilling to help them, so they must solve the mystery on their own.<br /><br />The main characters of this book are amazing, although there are so many it took me a long while to figure out which ones were which. Eventually, I got it, though. There is a fairly large amount of angst in everyone’s lives, perhaps maybe a bit too much to be realistic. But I grew up in a fairly sheltered environment, so I’m inclined to give the authors the benefit of the doubt. What’s truly amazing is that these characters are MORE than the problems that beset them and end up acting in very unexpected yet very human ways.<br /><br />I also always enjoy a good mystery and that was set up very well here. We get introduced to the weirdness going on slowly, to increase the suspense. But despite the book being well beyond 500 pages, I never felt like the story was lagging. Twist after twist was revealed, and I have to say that I guessed few of them. And, indeed, one of my guesses was dead wrong. The identity of the murderer came out of left field, but makes sense in retrospect. <br /><br />Another thing that makes this book so amazing is the authors’ willingness to subvert classic YA tropes. There’s some romance in this book, and some of it is healthy and some of it is unhealthy. Amazingly, the unhealthy romance is pointed out, not presented as actually healthy. Most significantly, while some of the main characters lead highly alternative lifestyles, I never felt like the authors were judging them one way or the other. And, of course, the authors aren’t afraid to drop real bombshells and change what you thought you knew about the characters.<br /><br />PLEASE read this book. You won’t regret it if you do. It’s rare that various elements – especially elements like these – are put together so well, but it happened. And I’m glad it did. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16018498824529385264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_462876927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/462876927" />
    <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy"><img alt="All Things Urban Fantasy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320345194p2/2732683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/462876927?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="All Things Urban Fantasy" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy">All Things Urban Fantasy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781468306583" href="/book/show/16101193-the-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy?shelf=reviewed-by-chris">reviewed-by-chris</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462876927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2695660373427661300">REVIEW COURTESY OF ALL THINGS URBAN FANTASY<br/><br/>When I was first asked if I wanted to review THE CIRCLE my first thought was whether or not is a based on the TV show THE SECRET CIRCLE. Thanks to Google I found out that it was most definitely not based on the TV show – which was apparently based on a different series of books. Oops. THE CIRCLE sure shares a lot in common with THE SECRET CIRCLE (or at least with the few episodes of the show I’ve seen), but it stands well enough on its own.<br/><br/>THE CIRCLE re</span>
  <span id="freeText2695660373427661300" style="display:none">REVIEW COURTESY OF ALL THINGS URBAN FANTASY<br /><br />When I was first asked if I wanted to review THE CIRCLE my first thought was whether or not is a based on the TV show THE SECRET CIRCLE. Thanks to Google I found out that it was most definitely not based on the TV show – which was apparently based on a different series of books. Oops. THE CIRCLE sure shares a lot in common with THE SECRET CIRCLE (or at least with the few episodes of the show I’ve seen), but it stands well enough on its own.<br /><br />THE CIRCLE revolves around seven high schoolers who are chosen to protect the Swedish town of Engelfors from evil forces. The evil started with some bodiless demons and only gets worse for the group from there. As the story progresses each of the girls develop (or are granted) various powers that help them in this fight.<br /><br />Sounds like a ton of other books you’ve read before, right? And, honestly, it is. There’s not a whole lot of originality in the plot of THE CIRCLE. What makes this book stand out a bit from the rest of the pack are the characters. These girls are all different and the complexities of their relationships kept me turning the pages long after I’d lost interest in the “main” plot line. You’ve got family issues, emotional blackmail, rivalries, regretted sexual entanglements and a whole lot more. I swear this book isn’t as soap operaish as that last sentence made it sound. The authors did an excellent job with dialog and fleshing out the individual girls – which made the lazy paranormal plot all the more irritating.<br /><br />While I applaud the authors’ willingness to kill off any character it often felt like the decision was done solely to shock. Plus watching them call in the calvary of adult witches to explain everything at the end caused some considerable eye-rolling on my part.<br /><br />As THE CIRCLE is the first in a series it did lay just enough groundwork that I’m curious to see where it goes next. If the authors focus as much on the plot as they do on the characterization in book two this could turn in to an excellent YA series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2695660373427661300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_637702367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/637702367" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/344678-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268032468p2/344678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/637702367?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/344678-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781468306583" href="/book/show/16101193-the-circle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer637702367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2511751448336337993">I like this series quite a bit, I guess you could call me a fan as I've been following the authors' work and have seen them talk about the books multiple times now. It has its flaws but I love the Swedish setting and the detailed descriptions of teen life.<br/><br/>I bought the English translation as a present for a teen and decided to reread it to see how it compares with the original. At first it was really weird reading about these characters in English, but I got used to it. I didn't love the translat</span>
  <span id="freeText2511751448336337993" style="display:none">I like this series quite a bit, I guess you could call me a fan as I've been following the authors' work and have seen them talk about the books multiple times now. It has its flaws but I love the Swedish setting and the detailed descriptions of teen life.<br /><br />I bought the English translation as a present for a teen and decided to reread it to see how it compares with the original. At first it was really weird reading about these characters in English, but I got used to it. I didn't love the translation, however. For the most part it was decent, but once in a while I would react to something that came off as sloppy. This is the version that's supposed to be sold in the states, and I got the feeling that they just changed a couple words from the British version and missed a couple things. I also felt that while some translations were technically correct they felt unnatural as a native speaker. I kept going back to my other copy to see what was said in Swedish!<br /><br />The first time I read Cirkeln I didn't mind the length, I got into the story and enjoyed the everydayness of it. Since I knew what was going to happen this time around I honestly got a little bored after about 200 pages. The story picks up again about 300 pages in, though. It's a little weird the way the story drags on through months and months without much progress, but I still don't want to lose any of the storylines. I really do love these characters. I was never bothered by the stereotypes that others complain about. I personally feel that they start out oversimplified in each other's eyes but eventually grow as you get to know them and they get to know each other. <br /><br />(First read in Swedish: April 20, 2012 - May 1, 2012, 3 stars)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2511751448336337993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wQSNMzwx+UL4ma+1AOYu1rHBuqvc4mFJTXh6PqxiFvRAiyNzjiBFC2HhMYoB21vW24nvKJQ8Fa6y8URZEDTUwQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UisVx6oiaRcE7cAYN2bbWChf4g7sP/MI1Uq54OGNftzTpLuHGDPVXp2VXic2W65YQhe3jaThh+8qw4eHXdu86Q==')})
  }
//]]>
